(function AMCV_patch(limit) {
  var current_cookie = document.cookie.match(/AMCV_[^=]*=MCMID\|[^;]*/g),
      value = current_cookie ? current_cookie[0].split("="):"",
      cookieParams = ";path=/;domain=ieee.org";

//      console.log("]*********** cookie: " + value);

  limit = limit ? limit:1;

  if ( value && value[1] ) {
    //AMCV cookie exists with value
    if ( (/\|/gi).test(value[1]) ) {
    //AMCV cookie contains |
//      console.log("]*********** found | in cookie: " + value[1]);
      document.cookie = value[0] + "=" + (value[1].replace(/\|/g,"%7C")) + cookieParams
    }
  } else {
    //AMCV cookie does not exist
//    console.log("]*********** found no cookie ");
    var consent = document.querySelector("[aria-label='Cookie Consent Banner']");
    if ( consent && !(/--hidden/gi).test(consent.classList) ){
    //Consent banner is active

      var observer = new MutationObserver((mutations) => {
        mutations.forEach((mutation) => {
//      console.log("]*********** consent banner mutation: " + mutation.attributeName);
          if ( mutation.attributeName == "class") {
//      console.log("]*********** run Patch");
            AMCV_patch();
          }
        });
      })
      observer.observe(consent, {
        subtree: false,
        childList: false,
        attributeFilter: ["class"],
        attributes: true
      });
    } else {
    //Consent banner is not active, cookie is not set
//      console.log("]*********** consent banner hidden, limit: " + limit);
      limit++;
      if( limit < 13 ) {
//      console.log("]*********** loop, limit: " + limit);
        clearTimeout(poll);
        var poll = setTimeout(AMCV_patch,500,limit)
      } else {
//      console.log("]*********** loop, past limit: " + limit);

//          console.log("]*********** click event");

                AMCV_patch();
              }
        }
        document.addEventListener("mousedown",sidebar);
      }
    }
  }
})();

xplmathjax="" xplhighlight="">Meta-learning methods are shown to be effective in quickly adapting a model to novel tasks. Most existing meta-learning methods represent data and carry out fast adaptation in euclidean space. In fact, data of real-world applications usually resides in complex and various Riemannian manifolds. emotion-eliciting stimuli is intrinsic to human vision. In this research, we investigate how emotion-elicitation features of images relate to human selective attention. We create the EMOtional attention dataset (EMOd). It is a set of diverse emotion-eliciting images, each with (1) eye-tracking data from 16 subjects, (2) image context labels at both object- and scene-level....</span><!----><a
